	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Anguilla</h1>

Bradley</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;<a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Anguilla" title="Premier of Anguilla">Premier</a> </div></th><td><a href="/wiki/Victor_Banks" title="Victor Banks">Victor Banks</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;<a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">UK government</a> minister </div></th><td><a href="/wiki/Tariq_Ahmad,_Baron_Ahmad_of_Wimbledon" title="Tariq Ahmad, Baron Ahmad of Wimbledon">Tariq Ahmad</a></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Legislature</th><td><a href="/wiki/Anguilla_House_of_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Anguilla House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Anguilla" title="Geography of Anguilla">Area</a></th></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;2011&#160;census</div></th><td>13,452</td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div million<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Data_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Data-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Per capita</div></th><td>$29,493.3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_dollar" postcode</a></th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code">AI-2640</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date format</th><td>dd/mm/yyyy</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Area_code_264" title="Area code 264">264</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:AI" title="ISO 3166-2:AI">AI</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.ai" title=".ai">.ai</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Anguilla</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">ann-<span style="font-size:90%">GWIL</span>-ə</i></a>) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British overseas territory</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Introduction_::Anguilla_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Introduction_::Anguilla-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It is one of the most northerly of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, lying east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a> and directly north of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The territory consists of the main island of Anguilla, approximately 16 miles (26&#160;km) long by 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) wide at its widest point, together with a number of much smaller islands and <a href="/wiki/Cay" title="Cay">cays</a> with no permanent population. The territory's capital is <a href="/wiki/The_Valley,_Anguilla" title="The Valley, Anguilla">The Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The total land area of the territory is 35 square miles (91&#160;km<sup>2</sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-facts_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> with a population of approximately 17,400 (July 2018 est.).<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name Anguilla is from the Italian <i><i lang="it" title="Italian language text">anguilla</i></i> meaning "<a href="/wiki/Eel" title="Eel">eel</a>" (in turn from the Latin <i>anguilla</i>, diminutive of <i>anguis</i>, snake) in reference to the island's shape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1839_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1839-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It is believed by most sources to have been named by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELaw1999_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELaw1999-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> For similar reasons, it was also known as <i>Snake</i> or <i>Snake Island</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1839_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1839-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1878_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1878-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEB1911_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEB1911-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Anguilla" title="History of Anguilla">History of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wallblake_House,_The_Valley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg/220px-Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg/330px-Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg/440px-Wallblake_House%2C_The_Valley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="882" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wallblake_House,_The_Valley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wallblake_House" title="Wallblake House">Wallblake House</a>, a plantation house thought to be the oldest building in Anguilla</div></div></div>
<p>Anguilla was first settled by Indigenous Amerindian peoples who migrated from South America.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  The earliest Native American artefacts found on Anguilla have been dated to around 1300&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>; remains of settlements date from <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">AD</span></span>&#160;600.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gov_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The native <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> name for the island was <i>Malliouhana</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Precisely when Anguilla was first seen by Europeans is uncertain: some sources claim that <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a> sighted the island during his second voyage in 1493, while others state that the first European explorer was the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a> Huguenot nobleman and merchant <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Goulaine_de_Laudonni%C3%A8re" title="René Goulaine de Laudonnière">René Goulaine de Laudonnière</a> in 1564.<sup id="cite_ref-gov_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> established a fort on the island in 1631, however later withdrew after it was destroyed by the Spanish in 1633.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Traditional accounts state that Anguilla was first colonised by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> settlers from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> beginning in 1650.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMartin1839_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMartin1839-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The settlers focused on planting tobacco, and to a lesser extent cotton.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  The French temporarily took over the island in 1666 but returned it to English control under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breda_(1667)" title="Treaty of Breda (1667)">Treaty of Breda</a> the next year.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>  A Major John Scott who visited in September 1667, wrote of leaving the island "in good condition" and noted that in July 1668, "200 or 300 people fled thither in time of war".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The French latter attacked again in 1688, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Anguilla" title="Battle of Anguilla">1745</a> and 1798, causing much destruction but failing to capture the island.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gov_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is likely that the early Europeans settlers brought enslaved Africans with them. Historians confirm that <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">African slaves</a> lived in the region in the early 17th century' for example, Africans from <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> were living on St Kitts in 1626.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> By 1672 a slave depot existed on the island of <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>, serving the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> While the time of African arrival in Anguilla is difficult to place precisely, archival evidence indicates a substantial African presence of at least 100 enslaved people by 1683; these seem to have come from Central Africa as well as West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Walicek,_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walicek,_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The slaves were forced to work on the sugar plantations which had begun to replace tobacco as Anguilla's main crop.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Over time the African slaves and their descendants came to vastly outnumber the white settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The African slave trade was eventually terminated within the British Empire in 1807, and slavery outlawed completely in 1834.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Many planters subsequently sold up or left the island.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>During the early colonial period, Anguilla was administered by the British through Antigua; in 1825, it was placed under the administrative control of nearby Saint Kitts.<sup id="cite_ref-gov_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gov-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Anguilla was federated with St Kitts and Nevis in 1882, against the wishes of many Anguillians.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Economic stagnation, and the severe effects of several droughts in the 1890s and later the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of the 1930s led many Anguillians to emigrate for better prospects elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Anguilla_(1967-1969).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flag_of_Anguilla_%281967-1969%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Anguilla_%281967-1969%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flag_of_Anguilla_%281967-1969%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Anguilla_%281967-1969%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flag_of_Anguilla_%281967-1969%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Anguilla_%281967-1969%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Anguilla_(1967-1969).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the short-lived Republic of Anguilla</div></div></div>
<p>Full adult suffrage was introduced to Anguilla in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> After a brief period as part of the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> (1958–62), the island of Anguilla became part of the <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts-Nevis-Anguilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Kitts-Nevis-Anguilla">Saint Kitts-Nevis-Anguilla</a> with full internal autonomy in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> However many Anguillians had no wish to be a part of this union, and resented the dominance of St Kitts within it. On 30 May 1967 Anguillians forcibly ejected the St Kitts police force from the island and declared their separation from St Kitts following a <a href="/wiki/1967_Anguillan_separation_referendum" title="1967 Anguillan separation referendum">referendum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DD_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The events, led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlin_Harrigan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Atlin Harrigan (page does not exist)">Atlin Harrigan</a><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Webster" title="Ronald Webster">Ronald Webster</a> amongst others, became known as the Anguillian Revolution; its goal was not independence per se, but rather independence from Saint Kitts and Nevis and a return to being a British colony. 
</p><p>With negotiations failing to break the deadlock, a <a href="/wiki/1969_Anguillan_constitutional_referendum" title="1969 Anguillan constitutional referendum">second referendum</a> confirming Anguillians' desire for separation from St Kitts was held and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Anguilla" title="Republic of Anguilla">Republic of Anguilla</a> was declared unilaterally, with Ronald Webster as President. Efforts by British envoy <a href="/wiki/William_Whitlock_(politician)" title="William Whitlock (politician)">William Whitlock</a> failed to break the impasse and 300 British troops were subsequently sent in March 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> British authority was restored, and confirmed by the Anguilla Act of July 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 1980 Anguilla was finally allowed to formally secede from Saint Kitts and Nevis and become a separate British <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">Crown colony</a> (now a <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Introduction_::Anguilla_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Introduction_::Anguilla-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Since then Anguilla has been politically stable, and has seen a large growth in its tourism and offshore financing sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_geology">Geography and geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography and geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Anguilla" title="Geography of Anguilla">Geography of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg/220px-Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg/330px-Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg/440px-Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3672" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anguilla-aerial_view_western_portion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An aerial view of the western portion of the island of Anguilla. The Blowing Point ferry terminal is visible in the lower right, as are (right to left) Shaddick Point, Rendezvous Bay, Cove Bay and Maundays Bay.</div></div></div>
<p>Anguilla is a flat, low-lying island of <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, measuring some 16m (26km) long and 3.5m (6km) in width.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>  It lies to the east of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Islands" title="Virgin Islands">Virgin Islands</a> and directly north of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a>, separated from that island by the <a href="/wiki/Anguilla_Channel" title="Anguilla Channel">Anguilla Channel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The soil is generally thin and poor, supporting scrub, tropical and forest vegetation.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The terrain is generally low-lying, with the highest terrain located in the vicinity of The Valley; <a href="/wiki/Crocus_Hill" title="Crocus Hill">Crocus Hill</a>, Anguilla's highest peak at 73m, lies in the western regions of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Anguilla, an island with 16,373 inhabitants, is a British Overseas Territory. <sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anguilla is noted for its ecologically important <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> and beaches. Apart from the main island of Anguilla itself, the territory includes a number of other smaller islands and <a href="/wiki/Cays" class="mw-redirect" title="Cays">cays</a>, mostly tiny and uninhabited:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Anguillita" title="Anguillita">Anguillita</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blowing_Rock,_Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Blowing Rock, Anguilla (page does not exist)">Blowing Rock</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dog_Island,_Anguilla" title="Dog Island, Anguilla">Dog Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Little_Scrub_Island" title="Little Scrub Island">Little Scrub Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prickly_Pear_Cays" title="Prickly Pear Cays">Prickly Pear Cays</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scrub_Island,_Anguilla" title="Scrub Island, Anguilla">Scrub Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seal_Island,_Anguilla" title="Seal Island, Anguilla">Seal Island</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sombrero,_Anguilla" title="Sombrero, Anguilla">Sombrero</a>, also known as Hat Island</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sandy_Island,_Anguilla" title="Sandy Island, Anguilla">Sandy Island</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Anguilla has a volcanic origin<sup id="cite_ref-PRINCETON_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRINCETON-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and has been submerged repeatedly from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<table>

<tbody><tr valign="top">

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SSS_Islands_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/SSS_Islands_Map.png/300px-SSS_Islands_Map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="386" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/SSS_Islands_Map.png/450px-SSS_Islands_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/SSS_Islands_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="527" data-file-height="678" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SSS_Islands_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing location of Anguilla relative to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Sint Maarten/Saint Martin</a> and other islands to its south</div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Anguilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Anguilla">Climate of Anguilla</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature">Temperature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Temperature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Northeastern trade winds keep this tropical island relatively cool and dry. Average annual temperature is 80&#160;°F (27&#160;°C).<sup id="cite_ref-facts_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> July–October is its hottest period, December–February, its coolest.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rainfall">Rainfall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Rainfall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Rainfall averages 35 inches (890&#160;mm) annually,<sup id="cite_ref-facts_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> although the figures vary from season to season and year to year. The island is subject to both sudden tropical storms and hurricanes, which occur in the period from July to November. The island suffered damage in 1995 from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> and severe flooding 5–20 feet from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">Political system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Political system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Anguilla" title="Politics of Anguilla">Politics of Anguilla</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Anguilla" title="Law of Anguilla">Law of Anguilla</a></div>
<p>Anguilla is an internally self-governing <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">overseas territory</a> of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Its politics take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependency</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Anguilla" title="Premier of Anguilla">Premier</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pluriform" class="extiw" title="wikt:pluriform">pluriform</a> multi-party system.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Committee_on_Decolonization" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Committee on Decolonization">United Nations Committee on Decolonization</a> includes Anguilla on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories</a>. The territory's constitution is the Anguilla Constitutional Order 1 April 1982 (amended 1990).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government, with <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a> being vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/Anguilla_House_of_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Anguilla House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defence">Defence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Defence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a dependency of the UK, the UK is responsible for Anguilla's military defence<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>, although there are no active <a href="/wiki/Garrisons" class="mw-redirect" title="Garrisons">garrisons</a> or armed forces present. Anguilla has a small <a href="/wiki/Marine_police" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine police">marine police</a> force, comprising around 32 personnel, which operates one <a href="/wiki/VT_Group" title="VT Group">VT Halmatic</a> M160-class 52-foot fast <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol boat</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Anguilla" title="Demographics of Anguilla">Demographics of Anguilla</a></div>
<p>The majority of residents (90.08%) are black, most of whom are the descendants of slaves transported from Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  Minorities include whites at 3.74% and people of mixed race at 4.65% (figures from 2001 census).
</p><p>72% of the population is Anguillian while 28% is non-Anguillian (2001 census). Of the non-Anguillian population, many are citizens of the United States, United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/St_Kitts_%26_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="St Kitts &amp; Nevis">St Kitts &amp; Nevis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>2006 and 2007 saw an influx of large numbers of Chinese, Indian and <a href="/wiki/Mexican_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican people">Mexican</a> workers, brought in as labour for major tourist developments due to the local population not being large enough to support the labour requirements.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Christian churches did not have a consistent or strong presence during the initial period of English colonisation; spiritual and religious practices of Europeans and Africans tended to reflect their regional origins. As early as 1813, Christian ministers formally ministered to enslaved Africans and promoted literacy among converts.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Wesleyan">Wesleyan</a> (Methodist) <a href="/wiki/Missionary_Society_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Missionary Society of England">Missionary Society of England</a> built churches and schools  from 1817.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2001 census, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is Anguilla's predominant religion, with 29% of the population practising <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a> and another 23.9% are <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>  Other churches on the island include <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventist">Seventh-day Adventist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> (served by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Saint_John%27s%E2%80%93Basseterre" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Saint John&#39;s–Basseterre">Diocese of Saint John's–Basseterre</a>, with the See at Saint John on <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>) and a small community of <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.7%).<sup id="cite_ref-statistics_census_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics_census-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Between 1992 and 2001 the number of followers of the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_God_(Cleveland,_Tennessee)" title="Church of God (Cleveland, Tennessee)">Church of God</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> increased considerably.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are at least 15 churches on the island. Although a minority on the island, Anguilla is an important location to followers of <a href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafarian</a> religion as the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Athlyi_Rogers" title="Robert Athlyi Rogers">Robert Athlyi Rogers</a>, author of the <i><a href="/wiki/Holy_Piby" title="Holy Piby">Holy Piby</a></i> which had a strong influence on Rastafarian and other Africa-centre belief systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Introduction_&amp;_Analysis_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Introduction_&amp;_Analysis-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Price2009_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Price2009-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> More recently, a Muslim cultural centre has opened on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics_census_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics_census-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anguillian_Creole" title="Anguillian Creole">Anguillian Creole</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg/220px-Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg/330px-Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg/440px-Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="372" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Ground_Anguilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Overlooking <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Ground,_Anguilla" title="Sandy Ground, Anguilla">Sandy Ground</a>, Anguilla</div></div></div>
<p>Today most people in Anguilla speak a British-influenced variety of standard <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Other languages are also spoken on the island, including varieties of Spanish, Chinese and the languages of other immigrant communities. However, the most common language other than Standard English is the island's own English-lexifier Creole language (not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Antillean_Creole" title="Antillean Creole">Antillean Creole</a> ('French Creole'), spoken in French islands such as <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>). It is referred to locally by terms such as "dialect" (pronounced "dialek"), Anguilla Talk or "Anguillian".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> It has its main roots in early varieties of English and West African languages, and is similar to the dialects spoken in English-speaking islands throughout the Eastern Caribbean in terms of its structural features.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Linguists who are interested in the origins of Anguillian and other Caribbean Creoles point out that some of its grammatical features can be traced to African languages while others can be traced to European languages. Three areas have been identified as significant for the identification of the linguistic origins of those forced migrants who arrived before 1710: the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast_(region)" title="Gold Coast (region)">Gold Coast</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Slave_Coast_of_West_Africa" title="Slave Coast of West Africa">Slave Coast</a> and the Windward Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sociohistorical information from Anguilla's archives suggest that Africans and Europeans formed two distinct, but perhaps overlapping speech communities in the early phases of the island's colonisation. "Anguillian" is believed to have emerged as the language of the masses as time passed, slavery was abolished and locals began to see themselves as "belonging" to Anguillian society.<sup id="cite_ref-Walicek,_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walicek,_Don_E_2009._pp._349-372-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Anguilla" title="Education in Anguilla">Education in Anguilla</a></div>
<p>There are six government primary schools, one government secondary school (<a href="/wiki/Albena_Lake_Hodge_Comprehensive_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Albena Lake Hodge Comprehensive School">Albena Lake Hodge Comprehensive School</a>), and two private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-schools_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schools-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> There is a single library, the Edison L. Hughes Education &amp; Library Complex of the Anguilla Public Library.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> A branch of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_James_School_of_Medicine" title="Saint James School of Medicine">Saint James School of Medicine</a> was established in 2011 in Anguilla.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a>, <a href="/wiki/For-profit_school" class="mw-redirect" title="For-profit school">for-profit</a> medical school headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Park_Ridge,_Illinois" title="Park Ridge, Illinois">Park Ridge</a>, Illinois.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> Open campus site in the island.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg/220px-Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg/330px-Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg/440px-Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cap_Juluca_-_Anguilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The beach at the Cap Juluca resort on Maundays Bay</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg/220px-Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="324" data-file-height="243" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sailing-in-anguilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A modern <a href="/wiki/Square_rigger" class="mw-redirect" title="Square rigger">square rigger</a> viewed from Long Bay</div></div></div>
<p>The island's cultural history begins with the native <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Taíno people">Taino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">Carib</a>. Their artefacts have been found around the island, telling of life before European settlers arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Anguilla National Trust (ANT) was established in 1988 and opened its offices in 1993 charged with the responsibility of preserving the heritage of the island, including its cultural heritage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> 
</p><p>As throughout the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, holidays are a cultural fixture. Anguilla's most important holidays are of historic as much as cultural importance – particularly the anniversary of the emancipation (previously August Monday in the Park), celebrated as the Summer Festival, or Carnival.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>  British festivities, such as the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Official_Birthday" title="Queen&#39;s Official Birthday">Queen's Birthday</a>, are also celebrated.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anguillian_cuisine" title="Anguillian cuisine">Anguillian cuisine</a></div>
<p>Anguillian cuisine is influenced by native Caribbean, African, Spanish, French and English cuisines.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Seafood is abundant, including prawns, shrimp, crab, <a href="/wiki/Spiny_lobster" title="Spiny lobster">spiny lobster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conch" title="Conch">conch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahi-mahi" title="Mahi-mahi">mahi-mahi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutjanus_campechanus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutjanus campechanus">red snapper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marlin" title="Marlin">marlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grouper" title="Grouper">grouper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Salt_cod" class="mw-redirect" title="Salt cod">Salt cod</a> is a staple food eaten on its own and used in stews, casseroles and soups.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Livestock is limited due to the small size of the island and people there use poultry, pork, goat and mutton, along with imported beef.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Goat is the most commonly eaten meat, used in a variety of dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A significant amount of the island's produce is imported due to limited land suitable for agriculture production; much of the soil is sandy and infertile.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Among the agriculture produced in Anguilla includes tomatoes, <a href="/wiki/Bell_pepper" title="Bell pepper">peppers</a>, limes and other <a href="/wiki/Citrus_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus fruit">citrus fruits</a>, onion, garlic, squash, <a href="/wiki/Pigeon_pea" title="Pigeon pea">pigeon peas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Callaloo" title="Callaloo">callaloo</a>. Starch staple foods include imported rice and other foods that are imported or locally grown, including <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NewYorkTimes_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewYorkTimes-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> sweet potatoes<sup id="cite_ref-NewYorkTimes_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewYorkTimes-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UsaToday_77-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UsaToday-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Anguilla National Trust has programmes encouraging Anguillian writers and the preservation of the island's history. In 2015, <i>Where I See The Sun – Contemporary Poetry in Anguilla</i> A New Anthology by <a href="/wiki/Lasana_M._Sekou" title="Lasana M. Sekou">Lasana M. Sekou</a> was published by House of Nehesi Publishers.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Among the forty three poets in the collection are Rita Celestine-Carty, <a href="/wiki/Bankie_Banx" title="Bankie Banx">Bankie Banx</a>, John T. Harrigan, <a href="/wiki/Patricia_J._Adams" title="Patricia J. Adams">Patricia J. Adams</a>, Fabian Fahie, Dr. Oluwakemi Linda Banks, and Reuel Ben Lewi.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Anguilla" title="Music of Anguilla">Music of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BankieBanx.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/BankieBanx.jpg/220px-BankieBanx.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/BankieBanx.jpg/330px-BankieBanx.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/BankieBanx.jpg/440px-BankieBanx.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4372" data-file-height="2906" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BankieBanx.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bankie_Banx" title="Bankie Banx">Bankie Banx</a>, noted reggae artist and poet from Anguilla who has built up an international following</div></div></div>
<p>Various Caribbean musical genres are popular on the island, such as <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sailing_in_Anguilla" title="Sailing in Anguilla">Sailing in Anguilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Anguilla" title="Rugby union in Anguilla">Rugby union in Anguilla</a></div>
<p>Boat racing has deep roots in Anguillian culture and is the national sport.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>  There are regular sailing <a href="/wiki/Regattas" class="mw-redirect" title="Regattas">regattas</a> on national holidays, such as Carnival, which are contested by locally built and designed boats. These boats have names and have sponsors that print their logo on their sails.
</p><p>As in many other former <a href="/wiki/British_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="British Colony">British colonies</a>, cricket is also a popular sport. Anguilla is the home of <a href="/wiki/Omari_Banks" title="Omari Banks">Omari Banks</a>, who played for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Cricket_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indies Cricket Team">West Indies Cricket Team</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Cardigan_Connor" title="Cardigan Connor">Cardigan Connor</a> played first-class cricket for English county side <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Hampshire County Cricket Club">Hampshire</a> and was 'chef de mission' (team manager) for Anguilla's <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> team in 2002. Other noted players include <a href="/wiki/Chesney_Hughes" title="Chesney Hughes">Chesney Hughes</a>, who plays for Derbyshire in England.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is represented in Anguilla by the Anguilla Eels RFC, who were formed in April 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The Eels have been finalists in the St. Martin tournament in November 2006 and semi-finalists in 2007, 2008, 2009 and Champions in 2010. The Eels were formed in 2006 by Scottish club national second row Martin Welsh, Club Sponsor and President of the AERFC Ms. Jacquie Ruan, and Canadian standout Scrumhalf Mark Harris (Toronto Scottish RFC).
</p><p>Anguilla is the birthplace of sprinter <a href="/wiki/Zharnel_Hughes" title="Zharnel Hughes">Zharnel Hughes</a> who has represented Great Britain since 2015, and England at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="2018 Commonwealth Games">2018 Commonwealth Games</a>. He won the 100 metres at the <a href="/wiki/2018_European_Athletics_Championships" title="2018 European Athletics Championships">2018 European Athletics Championships</a>, the 4 x 100 metres at the same championships, and the 4 x 100 metres for <a href="/wiki/England_at_the_2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="England at the 2018 Commonwealth Games">England at the 2018 Commonwealth Games</a>.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Shara_Proctor" title="Shara Proctor">Shara Proctor</a>, British Long Jump Silver Medalist in World Championships in Beijing first represented Anguilla in the event until 2010 when she began to represent Great Britain and England. Under the Anguillian Flag she achieved several medals in the <a href="/wiki/North_American,_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Athletic_Association" title="North American, Central American and Caribbean Athletic Association">NACAC</a> games.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Keith_Connor" title="Keith Connor">Keith Connor</a>, triple jumper, is also an Anguillian. He represented Great Britain and England and achieved several international titles including Commonwealth and European Games gold medals and an Olympic bronze medal. Keith later became Head Coach of Australia Athletics.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_history">Natural history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Natural history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuban_Tree_Frog_(Osteopilus_septentrionalis).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Cuban_Tree_Frog_%28Osteopilus_septentrionalis%29.jpg/220px-Cuban_Tree_Frog_%28Osteopilus_septentrionalis%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Cuban_Tree_Frog_%28Osteopilus_septentrionalis%29.jpg/330px-Cuban_Tree_Frog_%28Osteopilus_septentrionalis%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Cuban_Tree_Frog_%28Osteopilus_septentrionalis%29.jpg/440px-Cuban_Tree_Frog_%28Osteopilus_septentrionalis%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cuban_Tree_Frog_(Osteopilus_septentrionalis).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Cuban tree frog can be found on the island</div></div></div>
<p>Anguilla has habitat for the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_tree_frog" title="Cuban tree frog">Cuban tree frogs</a> (<i>Osteopilus septentrionalis</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Townsend_et_al._2000_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Townsend_et_al._2000-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Red-footed_tortoise" title="Red-footed tortoise">red-footed tortoise</a> (<i>Chelonoidis carbonaria</i>) is a species of tortoise found here, which originally came from South America.<sup id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Hurricanes led to over-water dispersal for the <a href="/wiki/Green_iguana" title="Green iguana">green iguanas</a> (<i>Iguana iguana</i>) to colonise Anguilla.<sup id="cite_ref-Censky_et_al._1998_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Censky_et_al._1998-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> All three animals are introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-Hailey_et_al._2011_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hailey_et_al._2011-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Five species of bats are known in the literature from Anguilla – the threatened <a href="/wiki/Insular_single_leaf_bat" title="Insular single leaf bat">insular single leaf bat</a> (<i>Monophyllus plethodon</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Antillean_fruit-eating_bat" title="Antillean fruit-eating bat">Antillean fruit-eating bat</a> (<i>Brachyphylla cavernarum</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Jamaican_fruit_bat" title="Jamaican fruit bat">Jamaican fruit bat</a> (<i>Artibeus jamaicensis</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_funnel-eared_bat" title="Mexican funnel-eared bat">Mexican funnel-eared bat</a> (<i>Natalus stramineus</i>), and the <a href="/wiki/Velvety_free-tailed_bat" title="Velvety free-tailed bat">velvety free-tailed bat</a> (<i>Molossus molossus</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Genoways_et_al.n2007_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genoways_et_al.n2007-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Anguilla" title="Economy of Anguilla">Economy of Anguilla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg/300px-Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg" decoding="async" width="300" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg/450px-Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg/600px-Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1033" data-file-height="810" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Anguilla.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2009 export percentages</div></div></div>
<p>Anguilla's thin arid soil being largely unsuitable for agriculture, the island has few land-based <a href="/wiki/Natural_resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural resources">natural resources</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Its main industries are tourism, <a href="/wiki/Offshore_companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore companies">offshore incorporation and management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Offshore_bank" title="Offshore bank">offshore banking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Captive_insurance" title="Captive insurance">captive insurance</a> and fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> &lt;/ref&gt;
</p><p>Anguilla's currency is the <a href="/wiki/East_Caribbean_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="East Caribbean dollar">East Caribbean dollar</a>, though the US dollar is also widely accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>  The exchange rate is fixed to the US dollar at US$1 = EC$2.70.
</p><p>The economy, and especially the tourism sector, suffered a setback in late 1995 due to the effects of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> in September. Hotels were hit particularly hard but a recovery occurred the following year. Another economic setback occurred during the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Before the 2008 worldwide crisis the economy of Anguilla was growing strongly, especially the tourism sector which was driving major new developments in partnerships with multi-national companies. Anguilla's tourism industry received a major boost when it was selected to host the <a href="/wiki/World_Travel_Awards" title="World Travel Awards">World Travel Awards</a> in December 2014. Known as "the Oscars of the travel industry", the awards ceremony was held at the <a href="/wiki/CuisinArt_Resort_and_Spa" title="CuisinArt Resort and Spa">CuisinArt Resort and Spa</a> and was hosted by <a href="/wiki/Vivica_A._Fox" title="Vivica A. Fox">Vivica A. Fox</a>. Anguilla was voted the World's Leading Luxury Island Destination from a short list of top-tier candidates such as St. Barts, the Maldives and Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anguilla's financial system comprises seven banks,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> two money services businesses, more than 40 company managers, more than 50 insurers, 12 brokers, more than 250 captive intermediaries, more than 50 mutual funds and eight trust companies.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anguilla has become a popular <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>, having no capital gains, estate, profit, sales, or corporate taxes. In April 2011, faced with a mounting deficit, it introduced a 3% "Interim Stabilisation Levy", Anguilla's first form of <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>. Anguilla also has a 0.75% property tax.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anguilla aims to obtain 15% of its energy from <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> to become less reliant on expensive imported diesel. The <a href="/wiki/Climate_%26_Development_Knowledge_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network">Climate &amp; Development Knowledge Network</a> is helping the government gather the information it needs to change the territory's legislation, so that it can integrate renewables into its grid. <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> has also made good progress in switching to renewables, but many other <a href="/wiki/Small_Island_Developing_States" title="Small Island Developing States">Small Island Developing States</a> are still at the early stages of planning how to integrate renewable energy into their grids. "For a small island we're very far ahead," said Beth Barry, Coordinator of the Anguilla Renewable Energy Office. "We've got an Energy Policy and a draft Climate Change policy and have been focussing efforts on the question of <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> supply for several years now. As a result, we have a lot of information we can share with other islands."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Anguilla" title="Transport in Anguilla">Transport in Anguilla</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wallblake_Airport_(Anguilla).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wallblake_Airport_%28Anguilla%29.jpg/220px-Wallblake_Airport_%28Anguilla%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wallblake_Airport_%28Anguilla%29.jpg/330px-Wallblake_Airport_%28Anguilla%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wallblake_Airport_%28Anguilla%29.jpg/440px-Wallblake_Airport_%28Anguilla%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wallblake_Airport_(Anguilla).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clayton J. Lloyd International Airport</div></div></div>
<p>Anguilla is served by <a href="/wiki/Clayton_J._Lloyd_International_Airport" title="Clayton J. Lloyd International Airport">Clayton J. Lloyd International Airport</a> (prior to 4 July 2010 known as Wallblake Airport). The primary runway at the airport is 5,462 feet (1,665&#160;m) in length and can accommodate moderate-sized aircraft. Services connect to various other Caribbean islands via regional carrier <a href="/wiki/LIAT" title="LIAT">LIAT</a>, local charter airlines and others. Although there are no direct scheduled flights to or from continental America or Europe, <a href="/wiki/Tradewind_Aviation" title="Tradewind Aviation">Tradewind Aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Air" title="Cape Air">Cape Air</a> provide scheduled air service to <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport">San Juan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. The airport can handle large <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body" class="mw-redirect" title="Narrow-body">narrow-body</a> jets such as the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing 727</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aside from taxis, there is no public transport on the island. Cars drive on the left.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boat">Boat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anguilla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Boat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are regular ferries from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> to Anguilla. It is a 20-minute crossing from <a href="/wiki/Marigot,_Saint_Martin" title="Marigot, Saint Martin">Marigot</a>, St. Martin to Blowing Point, Anguilla. Ferries commence service from 7:00&#160;am. There is also a charter service, from <a href="/wiki/Blowing_Point" class="mw-redirect" title="Blowing Point">Blowing Point</a>, Anguilla to <a href="/wiki/Princess_Juliana_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess Juliana Airport">Princess Juliana Airport</a> to make travel easier. This way of travel is the most common method of transport between Anguilla and St. Martin.
</p>
